<line act="1" scene="0" line="1" speaker="">I come no more to make you laugh: things now,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="2" speaker="">That bear a weighty and a serious brow,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="3" speaker="">Sad, high, and working, full of state and woe,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="4" speaker="">Such noble scenes as draw the eye to flow,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="5" speaker="">We now present. Those that can pity, here</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="6" speaker="">May, if they think it well, let fall a tear;</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="7" speaker="">The subject will deserve it. Such as give</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="8" speaker="">Their money out of hope they may believe,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="9" speaker="">May here find truth too. Those that come to see</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="10" speaker="">Only a show or two, and so agree</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="11" speaker="">The play may pass, if they be still and willing,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="12" speaker="">I'll undertake may see away their shilling</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="13" speaker="">Richly in two short hours. Only they</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="14" speaker="">That come to hear a merry bawdy play,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="15" speaker="">A noise of targets, or to see a fellow</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="16" speaker="">In a long motley coat guarded with yellow,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="17" speaker="">Will be deceived; for, gentle hearers, know,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="18" speaker="">To rank our chosen truth with such a show</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="19" speaker="">As fool and fight is, beside forfeiting</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="20" speaker="">Our own brains, and the opinion that we bring,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="21" speaker="">To make that only true we now intend,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="22" speaker="">Will leave us never an understanding friend.</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="23" speaker="">Therefore, for goodness' sake, and as you are known</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="24" speaker="">The first and happiest hearers of the town,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="25" speaker="">Be sad, as we would make ye: think ye see</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="26" speaker="">The very persons of our noble story</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="27" speaker="">As they were living; think you see them great,</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="28" speaker="">And follow'd with the general throng and sweat</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="29" speaker="">Of thousand friends; then in a moment, see</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="30" speaker="">How soon this mightiness meets misery:</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="31" speaker="">And, if you can be merry then, I'll say</line><line act="1" scene="0" line="32" speaker="">A man may weep upon his wedding-day.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="1" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Good morrow, and well met. How have ye done</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="2" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Since last we saw in France?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="3" speaker="NORFOLK">I thank your grace,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="4" speaker="NORFOLK">Healthful; and ever since a fresh admirer</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="5" speaker="NORFOLK">Of what I saw there.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="6" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">An untimely ague</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="7" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Stay'd me a prisoner in my chamber when</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="8" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Those suns of glory, those two lights of men,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="9" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Met in the vale of Andren.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="10" speaker="NORFOLK">'Twixt Guynes and Arde:</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="11" speaker="NORFOLK">I was then present, saw them salute on horseback;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="12" speaker="NORFOLK">Beheld them, when they lighted, how they clung</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="13" speaker="NORFOLK">In their embracement, as they grew together;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="14" speaker="NORFOLK">Which had they, what four throned ones could have weigh'd</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="15" speaker="NORFOLK">Such a compounded one?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="16" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">All the whole time</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="17" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">I was my chamber's prisoner.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="18" speaker="NORFOLK">Then you lost</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="19" speaker="NORFOLK">The view of earthly glory: men might say,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="20" speaker="NORFOLK">Till this time pomp was single, but now married</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="21" speaker="NORFOLK">To one above itself. Each following day</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="22" speaker="NORFOLK">Became the next day's master, till the last</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="23" speaker="NORFOLK">Made former wonders its. To-day the French,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="24" speaker="NORFOLK">All clinquant, all in gold, like heathen gods,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="25" speaker="NORFOLK">Shone down the English; and, to-morrow, they</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="26" speaker="NORFOLK">Made Britain India: every man that stood</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="27" speaker="NORFOLK">Show'd like a mine. Their dwarfish pages were</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="28" speaker="NORFOLK">As cherubins, all guilt: the madams too,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="29" speaker="NORFOLK">Not used to toil, did almost sweat to bear</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="30" speaker="NORFOLK">The pride upon them, that their very labour</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="31" speaker="NORFOLK">Was to them as a painting: now this masque</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="32" speaker="NORFOLK">Was cried incomparable; and the ensuing night</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="33" speaker="NORFOLK">Made it a fool and beggar. The two kings,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="34" speaker="NORFOLK">Equal in lustre, were now best, now worst,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="35" speaker="NORFOLK">As presence did present them; him in eye,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="36" speaker="NORFOLK">Still him in praise: and, being present both</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="37" speaker="NORFOLK">'Twas said they saw but one; and no discerner</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="38" speaker="NORFOLK">Durst wag his tongue in censure. When these suns--</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="39" speaker="NORFOLK">For so they phrase 'em--by their heralds challenged</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="40" speaker="NORFOLK">The noble spirits to arms, they did perform</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="41" speaker="NORFOLK">Beyond thought's compass; that former fabulous story,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="42" speaker="NORFOLK">Being now seen possible enough, got credit,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="43" speaker="NORFOLK">That Bevis was believed.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="44" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">O, you go far.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="45" speaker="NORFOLK">As I belong to worship and affect</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="46" speaker="NORFOLK">In honour honesty, the tract of every thing</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="47" speaker="NORFOLK">Would by a good discourser lose some life,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="48" speaker="NORFOLK">Which action's self was tongue to. the devil is a niggard,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="81" speaker="ABERGAVENNY">Or has given all before, and he begins</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="82" speaker="ABERGAVENNY">A new hell in himself.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="83" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Why the devil,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="84" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Upon this French going out, took he upon him,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="85" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Without the privity o' the king, to appoint</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="86" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Who should attend on him? A beggar's book</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="145" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Outworths a noble's blood.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="146" speaker="NORFOLK">What, are you chafed?</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="147" speaker="NORFOLK">Ask God for temperance; that's the appliance only</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="148" speaker="NORFOLK">Which your disease requires.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="149" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">I read in's looks</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="150" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Matter against me; and his eye reviled</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="151" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">Me, as his abject object: at this instant</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="152" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">He bores me with some trick: he's gone to the king;</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="153" speaker="BUCKINGHAM">I'll follow and outstare him.</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="154" speaker="NORFOLK">Stay, my lord,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="155" speaker="NORFOLK">And let your reason with your choler question</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="156" speaker="NORFOLK">What 'tis you go about: to climb steep hills</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="157" speaker="NORFOLK">Requires slow pace at first: anger is like</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="158" speaker="NORFOLK">A full-hot horse, who being allow'd his way,</line><line act="1" scene="1" line="159" speaker="NORFOLK">Self-mettle tires him. Attend.
